href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> and the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Nelson_149-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nelson-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Sovereign credit ratings represent an assessment by a rating agency of a sovereign\'s ability and willingness to repay its debt.<sup id="cite_ref-DNB_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DNB-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> The rating methodologies used to assess sovereign credit ratings are broadly similar to those used for corporate credit ratings, although the borrower\'s <i>willingness</i> to repay receives extra emphasis since national governments may be eligible for debt immunity under international law, thus complicating repayment obligations.<sup id="cite_ref-Caprio383_148-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Caprio383-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Nelson_149-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nelson-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> In addition, credit assessments reflect not only the long-term perceived default risk, but also short- or immediate-term political and economic developments.<sup id="cite_ref-Kolb_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kolb-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> Differences in sovereign ratings between agencies may reflect varying qualitative evaluations of the investment environment.<sup id="cite_ref-Iyengar_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Iyengar-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>National governments may solicit credit ratings to generate investor interest and improve access to the international capital markets.<sup id="cite_ref-Kolb_151-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kolb-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Iyengar_152-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Iyengar-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> Developing countries often depend on strong sovereign credit ratings to access funding in international bond markets.<sup id="cite_ref-Kolb_151-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kolb-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> Once ratings for a sovereign have been initiated, the rating agency will continue to monitor for relevant developments and adjust its credit opinion accordingly.<sup id="cite_ref-Kolb_151-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kolb-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A 2010 International Monetary Fund study concluded that ratings were a reasonably good indicator of sovereign-default risk.<sup id="cite_ref-GFSR_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GFSR-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Tenure_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tenure-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> However, credit rating agencies were criticized for failing to predict the <a href="/wiki/1997_Asian_financial_crisis" title="1997 Asian financial crisis">1997 Asian financial crisis</a> and for downgrading countries in the midst of that turmoil.<sup id="cite_ref-DNB_150-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DNB-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> Similar criticisms emerged after recent credit downgrades to Greece, Ireland, Portugal, and Spain,<sup id="cite_ref-DNB_150-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DNB-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> although credit ratings agencies had begun to downgrade peripheral <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">Eurozone</a> countries well before the <a href="/wiki/Eurozone_crisis" class="mw-redirect" title="Eurozone crisis">Eurozone crisis</a> began.<sup id="cite_ref-Tenure_153-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tenure-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Conflict_of_interest_in_assigning_sovereign_ratings">Conflict of interest in assigning sovereign ratings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Credit_rating_agency&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Conflict of interest in assigning sovereign ratings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>As part of the <a href="/wiki/Sarbanes%E2%80%93Oxley_Act" title="Sarbanes\xe2\x80\x93Oxley Act">Sarbanes\xe2\x80\x93Oxley Act</a> of 2002, Congress ordered the U.S. SEC to develop a report, titled "Report on the Role and Function of Credit Rating Agencies in the Operation of the Securities Markets"<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> detailing how credit ratings are used in U.S. regulation and the policy issues this use raises. Partly as a result of this report, in June 2003, the SEC published a "concept release" called "Rating Agencies and the Use of Credit Ratings under the Federal Securities Laws"<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> that sought public comment on many of the issues raised in its report.  Public comments on this concept release have also been published on the SEC\'s website.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In December 2004, the <a href="/wiki/International_Organization_of_Securities_Commissions" title="International Organization of Securities Commissions">International Organization of Securities Commissions</a> (IOSCO) published a Code of Conduct<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> for CRAs that, among other things, is designed to address the types of conflicts of interest that CRAs face. All of the major CRAs have agreed to sign on to this Code of Conduct and it has been praised by regulators ranging from the European Commission to the US SEC.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Use_by_government_regulators">Use by government regulators</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Credit_rating_agency&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Use by government regulators">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Nationally_recognized_statistical_rating_organization" title="Nationally recognized statistical rating organization">Nationally recognized statistical rating organization</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Basel_III" title="Basel III">Basel III</a></div>\n<p>Regulatory authorities and legislative bodies in the United States and other jurisdictions rely on credit rating agencies\' assessments of a broad range of debt issuers, and thereby attach a regulatory function to their ratings.<sup id="cite_ref-CaprioRegulation_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CaprioRegulation-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Jackson_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jackson-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> This regulatory role is a derivative function in that the agencies do not publish ratings for that purpose.<sup id="cite_ref-CaprioRegulation_158-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CaprioRegulation-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> Governing bodies at both the national and international level have woven credit ratings into \nminimum capital requirements for banks, allowable investment alternatives for many institutional investors, and similar restrictive regulations for insurance companies and other financial market participants.<sup id="cite_ref-WorldBankGlobalFinancial_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WorldBankGlobalFinancial-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Langohr_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Langohr-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The use of credit ratings by regulatory agencies is not a new phenomenon.<sup id="cite_ref-CaprioRegulation_158-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CaprioRegulation-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> In the 1930s, regulators in the United States used credit rating agency ratings to prohibit banks from investing in bonds that were deemed to be below <a href="/wiki/Investment_grade#Investment_grade" class="mw-redirect" title="Investment grade">investment grade</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-White_89-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-White-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>  In the following decades, state regulators outlined a similar role for agency ratings in restricting <a href="/wiki/Insurance#Insurance_companies" title="Insurance">insurance company</a> investments.<sup id="cite_ref-White_89-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-White-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CaprioRegulation_158-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CaprioRegulation-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> From 1975 to 2006, the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Securities_and_Exchange_Commission" title="U.S. Securities and Exchange Commission">U.S. Securities and Exchange Commission</a> (SEC) recognized the largest and most credible agencies as <a href="/wiki/Nationally_Recognized_Statistical_Rating_Organizations" class="mw-redirect" title="Nationally Recognized Statistical Rating Organizations">Nationally Recognized Statistical Rating Organizations</a>, and relied on such agencies exclusively for distinguishing between grades of creditworthiness in various regulations under federal securities laws.<sup id="cite_ref-CaprioRegulation_158-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CaprioRegulation-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Langohr409_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Langohr409-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Credit_Rating_Agency_Reform_Act" title="Credit Rating Agency Reform Act">Credit Rating Agency Reform Act</a> of 2006 created a voluntary registration system for CRAs that met a certain minimum criteria, and provided the SEC with broader oversight authority.<sup id="cite_ref-Alcubilla2_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Alcubilla2-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The practice of using credit rating agency ratings for regulatory purposes has since expanded globally.<sup id="cite_ref-CaprioRegulation_158-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CaprioRegulation-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> Today, financial market regulations in many countries contain extensive references to ratings.<sup id="cite_ref-CaprioRegulation_158-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CaprioRegulation-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Fuchita_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fuchita-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Basel_III" title="Basel III">Basel III</a> accord, a global bank capital standardization effort, relies on credit ratings to calculate minimum capital standards and minimum liquidity ratios.<sup id="cite_ref-CaprioRegulation_158-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CaprioRegulation-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The extensive use of credit ratings for regulatory purposes can have a number of unintended effects.<sup id="cite_ref-CaprioRegulation_158-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CaprioRegulation-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup>  Because regulated market participants must follow minimum investment grade provisions, ratings changes across the investment/non-investment grade boundary may lead to strong market price fluctuations and potentially cause systemic reactions.<sup id="cite_ref-CaprioRegulation_158-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CaprioRegulation-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> The regulatory function granted to credit rating agencies may also adversely affect their original market information function of providing credit opinions.<sup id="cite_ref-CaprioRegulation_158-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CaprioRegulation-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Langhor384_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Langhor384-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Against this background and in the wake of criticism of credit rating agencies following the <a href="/wiki/Subprime_mortgage_crisis" title="Subprime mortgage crisis">subprime mortgage crisis</a>, legislators in the United States and other jurisdictions have commenced to reduce rating reliance in laws and regulations.<sup id="cite_ref-White_89-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-White-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Alcubilla_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Alcubilla-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Dodd%E2%80%93Frank_Wall_Street_Reform_and_Consumer_Protection_Act" title="Dodd\xe2\x80\x93Frank Wall Street Reform and Consumer Protection Act">2010 Dodd\xe2\x80\x93Frank Act</a>  removes statutory references to credit rating agencies, and calls for federal regulators to review and modify existing regulations to avoid relying on credit ratings as the sole assessment of creditworthiness.<sup id="cite_ref-Skeel_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skeel-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Hawley_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hawley-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SECCRA_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SECCRA-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Industry_structure">Industry structure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Credit_rating_agency&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Industry structure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Big_Three_agencies">The Big Three agencies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Credit_rating_agency&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: The Big Three agencies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Credit rating is a highly concentrated industry, with the <a href="/wiki/Big_Three_(credit_rating_agencies)" title="Big Three (credit rating agencies)">"Big Three" credit rating agencies</a> controlling approximately 95% of the ratings business.<sup id="cite_ref-controversy_3-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-controversy-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Moody%27s_Investors_Service" title="Moody&#39;s Investors Service">Moody\'s Investors Service</a> and <a href="/wiki/Standard_%26_Poor%27s#Credit_ratings" title="Standard &amp; Poor&#39;s">Standard &amp; Poor\'s</a> (S&amp;P) together control 80% of the global market, and <a href="/wiki/Fitch_Ratings" title="Fitch Ratings">Fitch Ratings</a> controls a further 15%.<sup id="cite_ref-Baker_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Baker-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SECReport2012_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SECReport2012-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-controversy_3-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-controversy-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DW_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DW-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As of December 2012, S&amp;P is the largest of the three, with 1.2 million outstanding ratings and 1,416 analysts and supervisors;<sup id="cite_ref-SECReport2012_170-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SECReport2012-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NeumannFinancial_172-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NeumannFinancial-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> Moody\'s has 1 million outstanding ratings and 1,252 analysts and supervisors;<sup id="cite_ref-SECReport2012_170-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SECReport2012-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NeumannFinancial_172-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NeumannFinancial-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> and Fitch is the smallest, with approximately 350,000 outstanding ratings, and is sometimes used as an alternative to S&amp;P and Moody\xe2\x80\x99s.<sup id="cite_ref-SECReport2012_170-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SECReport2012-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The three largest agencies are not the only sources of credit information.<sup id="cite_ref-WhiteAltman_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WhiteAltman-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> Many smaller rating agencies also exist, mostly serving non-US markets.<sup id="cite_ref-LanghorSmall_174-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LanghorSmall-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> All of the large securities firms have internal <a href="/wiki/Securities_research" title="Securities research">fixed income analysts</a> who offer information about the risk and volatility of securities to their clients.<sup id="cite_ref-WhiteAltman_54-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WhiteAltman-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> And <a href="/wiki/Risk_management" title="Risk management">specialized risk consultants</a> working in a variety of fields offer credit models and default estimates.<sup id="cite_ref-WhiteAltman_54-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WhiteAltman-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Market share concentration is not a new development in the credit rating industry. Since the establishment of the first agency in 1909, there have never been more than four credit rating agencies with significant market share.<sup id="cite_ref-Caprio386_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Caprio386-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> Even the <a href="/wiki/Financial_crisis_of_2007%E2%80%9308" class="mw-redirect" title="Financial crisis of 2007\xe2\x80\x9308">Financial crisis of 2007\xe2\x80\x9308</a>\xe2\x80\x94where the performance of the three rating agencies was dubbed "horrendous" by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Economist" title="The Economist">The Economist</a></i> magazine<sup id="cite_ref-econ_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-econ-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup>\xe2\x80\x94led to a drop in the share of the three by just one percent\xe2\x80\x94from 98 to 97%.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The reason for the concentrated market structure is disputed. One widely cited opinion is that the Big Three\'s historical reputation within the financial industry creates a high barrier of entry for new entrants.<sup id="cite_ref-Caprio386_175-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Caprio386-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> Following the enactment of the <a href="/wiki/Credit_Rating_Agency_Reform_Act" title="Credit Rating Agency Reform Act">Credit Rating Agency Reform Act</a> of 2006 in the US, seven additional rating agencies attained recognition from the SEC as <a href="/wiki/Nationally_recognized_statistical_rating_organization" title="Nationally recognized statistical rating organization">nationally recognized statistical rating organization</a> (NRSROs).<sup id="cite_ref-CFO_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CFO-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SEC-NRSRO_179-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SEC-NRSRO-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> While these other agencies remain niche players,<sup id="cite_ref-FT-Cifuentes_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FT-Cifuentes-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> some have gained market share following the <a href="/wiki/Financial_crisis_of_2007%E2%80%9308" class="mw-redirect" title="Financial crisis of 2007\xe2\x80\x9308">Financial crisis of 2007\xe2\x80\x9308</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-MNI_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MNI-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> and in October 2012 several announced plans to join together and create a new organization called the Universal Credit Rating Group.<sup id="cite_ref-FT-Rabinovitch_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FT-Rabinovitch-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup>  The <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> has considered setting up a state-supported EU-based agency.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup> In November 2013, credit ratings organizations from five countries (CPR of Portugal, CARE Rating of India, GCR of South Africa, MARC of Malaysia, and SR Rating of Brazil) joint ventured to launch <a href="/w/index.php?title=ARC_Ratings&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="ARC Ratings (page does not exist)">ARC Ratings</a>, a new global agency touted as an alternative to the "Big Three".<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_credit_rating_agencies">Other credit rating agencies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Credit_rating_agency&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Other credit rating agencies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In addition to "the Big Three" of <a href="/wiki/Moody%27s" class="mw-redirect" title="Moody&#39;s">Moody\'s</a>, <a href="/wiki/Standard_%26_Poor%27s" title="Standard &amp; Poor&#39;s">Standard &amp; Poor\'s</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Fitch_Ratings" title="Fitch Ratings">Fitch Ratings</a>, other agencies and rating companies include:\n</p><p>DataPro Limited (Nigeria), Agusto &amp; Co. (Nigeria), <a href="/wiki/A._M._Best" title="A. M. Best">A. M. Best</a> (U.S.), <a href="/w/index.php?title=Capital_Intelligence_Ratings_Limited_(CIR)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Capital Intelligence Ratings Limited (CIR) (page does not exist)">Capital Intelligence Ratings Limited (CIR)</a> (Cyprus), <a href="/w/index.php?title=China_Lianhe_Credit_Rating_Co.,_Ltd.&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="China Lianhe Credit Rating Co., Ltd. (page does not exist)">China Lianhe Credit Rating Co., Ltd.</a> (China), <a href="/wiki/China_Chengxin_Credit_Rating_Group" title="China Chengxin Credit Rating Group">China Chengxin Credit Rating Group</a> (China), <a href="/w/index.php?title=Credit_Rating_Agency_Ltd&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Credit Rating Agency Ltd (page does not exist)">Credit Rating Agency Ltd</a> (Zambia), <a href="/wiki/Credit_Rating_Information_and_Services_Limited" title="Credit Rating Information and Services Limited">Credit Rating Information and Services Limited</a><sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> (Bangladesh), CTRISKS (Hong Kong),<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Dagong_Europe_Credit_Rating" title="Dagong Europe Credit Rating">Dagong Europe Credit Rating</a> (Italy), <a href="/wiki/DBRS" title="DBRS">DBRS</a> (Canada), <a href="/wiki/Dun_%26_Bradstreet" title="Dun &amp; Bradstreet">Dun &amp; Bradstreet</a> (U.S.), <a href="/wiki/Egan-Jones_Rating_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="Egan-Jones Rating Company">Egan-Jones Rating Company</a> (U.S.), Global Credit Ratings Co. (South Africa), HR Ratings de M\xc3\xa9xico, S.A. de C.V. (Mexico), <a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Pakistan_Credit_Rating_Agency_Limited_(PACRA)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="The Pakistan Credit Rating Agency Limited (PACRA) (page does not exist)">The Pakistan Credit Rating Agency Limited (PACRA)</a> (Pakistan), <a href="/wiki/ICRA_Limited" title="ICRA Limited">ICRA Limited</a> (India),\n<a href="/wiki/Japan_Credit_Rating_Agency" title="Japan Credit Rating Agency">Japan Credit Rating Agency</a><sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup> (Japan) ,JCR VIS Credit Rating Company Ltd (Pakistan), <a href="/wiki/Kroll_Bond_Rating_Agency" title="Kroll Bond Rating Agency">Kroll Bond Rating Agency</a> (U.S.), Levin and Goldstein (Zambia), modeFinance (Italy), <a href="/wiki/Morningstar,_Inc." title="Morningstar, Inc.">Morningstar, Inc.</a> (U.S.), Muros Ratings (Russia, alternative rating company), Public Sector Credit Solutions (U.S., not-for profit rating provider), <a href="/wiki/Rapid_Ratings_International" title="Rapid Ratings International">Rapid Ratings International</a> (U.S.), <a href="/wiki/RusRating" title="RusRating">RusRating</a> (Russia), <a href="/wiki/Universal_Credit_Rating_Group" title="Universal Credit Rating Group">Universal Credit Rating Group</a> (Hong Kong), <a href="/wiki/Veda_(company)" title="Veda (company)">Veda</a> (Australia, previously known as Baycorp Advantage), <a href="/wiki/Wikirating" title="Wikirating">Wikirating</a> (Switzerland, alternative rating organization), <a href="/w/index.php?title=Humphreys_Ltd_(company)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Humphreys Ltd (company) (page does not exist)">Humphreys Ltd</a> (Chile, previously known as Moody\'s partner in Chile), Credit Research Initiative<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> (Singapore, non-profit rating provider), Spread Research (independent credit research and rating agency, France), INC Rating (Poland).\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Business_models">Business models</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Credit_rating_agency&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Business models">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Credit rating agencies generate revenue from a variety of activities related to the production and distribution of credit ratings.<sup id="cite_ref-SECReportCongress_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SECReportCongress-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup> The sources of the revenue are generally the issuer of the securities or the investor. Most agencies operate under one or a combination of <a href="/wiki/Business_model" title="Business model">business models</a>: the <a href="/wiki/Subscription_business_model" title="Subscription business model">subscription model</a> and the issuer-pays model.<sup id="cite_ref-Caprio_49-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Caprio-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> However, agencies may offer additional services using a combination of business models.<sup id="cite_ref-SECReportCongress_190-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SECReportCongress-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Brinded_191-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brinded-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Under the subscription model, the credit rating agency does not make its ratings freely available to the market, so investors pay a subscription fee for access to ratings.<sup id="cite_ref-Caprio_49-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Caprio-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Pragyan_192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pragyan-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup> This revenue provides the main source of agency income, although agencies may also provide other types of services.<sup id="cite_ref-Caprio_49-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Caprio-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GeneralPrinciples_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GeneralPrinciples-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> Under the issuer-pays model, agencies charge issuers a fee for providing credit rating assessments.<sup id="cite_ref-Caprio_49-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Caprio-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> This revenue stream allows issuer-pays credit rating agencies to make their ratings freely available to the broader market, especially via the Internet.<sup id="cite_ref-Foley_194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Foley-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-IndiaTimes_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IndiaTimes-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The subscription approach was the prevailing business model until the early 1970s, when <a href="/wiki/Moody%27s_Investors_Service" title="Moody&#39;s Investors Service">Moody\'s</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fitch_Ratings" title="Fitch Ratings">Fitch</a>, and finally <a href="/wiki/Standard_%26_Poor%27s#Credit_ratings" title="Standard &amp; Poor&#39;s">Standard &amp; Poor\'s</a> adopted the issuer-pays model.<sup id="cite_ref-Caprio_49-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Caprio-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Pragyan_192-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pragyan-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup> Several factors contributed to this transition, including increased investor demand for credit ratings, and widespread use of information sharing technology\xe2\x80\x94such as <a href="/wiki/Fax_machines" class="mw-redirect" title="Fax machines">fax machines</a> and <a href="/wiki/Photocopier" title="Photocopier">photocopiers</a>\xe2\x80\x94which allowed investors to freely share agencies\xe2\x80\x99 reports and undermined demand for subscriptions.<sup id="cite_ref-Jiang_196-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jiang-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup> Today, eight of the nine <a href="/wiki/Nationally_recognized_statistical_rating_organization" title="Nationally recognized statistical rating organization">nationally recognized statistical rating organizations</a> (NRSRO) use the issuer-pays model, only <a href="/wiki/Egan-Jones" class="mw-redirect" title="Egan-Jones">Egan-Jones</a> maintains an investor subscription service.<sup id="cite_ref-Foley_194-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Foley-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup> Smaller, regional credit rating agencies may use either model. For example, China\'s oldest rating agency, Chengxin Credit Management Co., uses the issuer-pays model. The Universal Credit Ratings Group, formed by Beijing-based <a href="/wiki/Dagong_Global_Credit_Rating" title="Dagong Global Credit Rating">Dagong Global Credit Rating</a>, <a href="/wiki/Egan-Jones" class="mw-redirect" title="Egan-Jones">Egan-Jones</a> of the U.S. and Russia\xe2\x80\x99s RusRatings, uses the investor-pays model,<sup id="cite_ref-UCRG_197-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UCRG-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Hunt_198-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hunt-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Gaillard_199-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gaillard-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup> while <a href="/wiki/Dagong_Europe_Credit_Rating" title="Dagong Europe Credit Rating">Dagong Europe Credit Rating</a>, the other joint-venture of <a href="/wiki/Dagong_Global_Credit_Rating" title="Dagong Global Credit Rating">Dagong Global Credit Rating</a>, uses the issuer-pays model.\n</p><p>Critics argue that the issuer-pays model creates a potential conflict of interest because the agencies are paid by the organizations whose debt they rate.<sup id="cite_ref-Anderson_200-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Anderson-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup> However, the subscription model is also seen to have disadvantages, as it restricts the ratings\' availability to paying investors.<sup id="cite_ref-Foley_194-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Foley-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-IndiaTimes_195-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IndiaTimes-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> Issuer-pays CRAs have argued that subscription-models can also be subject to conflicts of interest due to pressures from investors with strong preferences on product ratings.<sup id="cite_ref-FSA-19_201-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FSA-19-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup> In 2010 Lace Financials, a subscriber-pays agency later acquired by <a href="/wiki/Kroll_Inc." title="Kroll Inc.">Kroll Ratings</a>, was fined by the SEC for violating securities rules to the benefit of its largest subscriber.<sup id="cite_ref-Neumann_202-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Neumann-202">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A 2009 <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> report proposed a "hybrid" approach in which issuers who pay for ratings are required to seek additional scores from subscriber-based third parties.<sup id="cite_ref-WorldBank_203-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WorldBank-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup> Other proposed alternatives include a "public-sector" model in which national governments fund the rating costs, and an "exchange-pays" model, in which stock and bond exchanges pay for the ratings.<sup id="cite_ref-FSA_204-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FSA-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SEBI_205-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SEBI-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup> Crowd-sourced, collaborative models such as <a href="/wiki/Wikirating" title="Wikirating">Wikirating</a> have been suggested as an alternative to both the subscription and issuer-pays models, although it is a recent development as of the 2010, and not yet widely used.<sup id="cite_ref-Greenwood_206-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Greenwood-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Yali_207-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yali-207">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Oligopoly_produced_by_regulation">Oligopoly produced by regulation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Credit_rating_agency&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Oligopoly produced by regulation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Agencies are sometimes accused of being <a href="/wiki/Oligopoly" title="Oligopoly">oligopolists</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup>  because barriers to market entry are high and rating agency business is itself reputation-based (and the finance industry pays little attention to a rating that is not widely recognized). In 2003, the US SEC submitted a report to Congress detailing plans to launch an investigation into the anti-competitive practices of credit rating agencies and issues including conflicts of interest.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Think_tank" title="Think tank">Think tanks</a> such as the <a href="/wiki/World_Pensions_%26_Investments_Forum" title="World Pensions &amp; Investments Forum">World Pensions Council (WPC)</a> have argued that the <a href="/wiki/Basel_II" title="Basel II">Basel II</a>/III \xe2\x80\x9ccapital adequacy\xe2\x80\x9d norms favored at first essentially by the <a href="/wiki/Central_bank" title="Central bank">central banks</a> of France, Germany and Switzerland (while the US and the UK were rather lukewarm) have unduly encouraged the use of ready-made opinions produced by oligopolistic rating agencies<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Of the large agencies, only Moody\'s is a separate, publicly held corporation that discloses its financial results without dilution by non-ratings businesses, and its high profit margins (which at times have been greater than 50 percent of gross margin) can be construed as consistent with the type of returns one might expect in an industry which has high barriers to entry.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup> Celebrated investor <a href="/wiki/Warren_Buffett" title="Warren Buffett">Warren Buffett</a> described the company as \xe2\x80\x9ca natural duopoly,\xe2\x80\x9d with  \xe2\x80\x9cincredible\xe2\x80\x9d pricing power, when asked by the Financial Crisis Inquiry Commission about his ownership of 15% of the company.<sup id="cite_ref-FCIR-p207_213-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FCIR-p207-213">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>According to professor <a href="/wiki/Frank_Partnoy" title="Frank Partnoy">Frank Partnoy</a>, the regulation of CRAs by the SEC and <a href="/wiki/Federal_Reserve_Bank" title="Federal Reserve Bank">Federal Reserve Bank</a> has eliminated competition between CRAs and practically forced market participants to use the services of the three big agencies, Standard and Poor\'s, Moody\'s and Fitch.<sup id="cite_ref-triple_215-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-triple-215">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>SEC Commissioner Kathleen Casey has said that these CRAs have acted much like Fannie Mae, Freddie Mac and other companies that dominate the market because of government actions. When the CRAs gave ratings that were "catastrophically misleading, the large rating agencies enjoyed their most profitable years ever during the past decade."<sup id="cite_ref-triple_215-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-triple-215">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>To solve this problem, Ms. Casey (and others such as NYU professor <a href="/wiki/Lawrence_J._White" title="Lawrence J. White">Lawrence White</a><sup id="cite_ref-oligopoly_216-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oligopoly-216">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup>) have proposed removing the NRSRO rules completely.<sup id="cite_ref-triple_215-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-triple-215">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup> Professor Frank Partnoy suggests that the regulators use the results of the credit risk swap markets rather than the ratings of NRSROs.<sup id="cite_ref-triple_215-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-triple-215">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The CRAs have made competing suggestions that would, instead, add further regulations that would make market entrance even more expensive than it is now.<sup id="cite_ref-oligopoly_216-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oligopoly-216">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Credit_rating_agency&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Nationally_recognized_statistical_rating_organization" title="Nationally recognized statistical rating organization">Nationally recognized statistical rating organization</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Securities_Industry_and_Financial_Markets_Association" title="Securities Industry and Financial Markets Association">Securities Industry and Financial Markets Association</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_credit_rating" title="List of countries by credit rating">List of countries by credit rating</a></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" GPO. 2011. p.&#160;119. <q>Credit ratings also determined whether investors could buy certain investments at all. National Commission on the Causes of the Financial and Economic Crisis in the United States. 2011. pp.&#160;43\xe2\x80\x9344. <q>Purchasers of the safer tranches got a higher rate of return than ultra-safe Treasury notes without much extra risk\xe2\x80\x94at least in theory. However, the financial engineering behind these investments made them harder to understand and to price than individual loans. To determine likely returns, investors had to calculate the statistical probabilities that certain kinds of mortgages might default, and to estimate the revenues that would be lost because of those defaults. Then investors had to determine the effect of the losses on the payments to different tranches. This complexity transformed the three leading credit rating agencies\xe2\x80\x94Moody\xe2\x80\x99s, Standard &amp; Poor\xe2\x80\x99s (S&amp;P), and Fitch\xe2\x80\x94into key players in the process, positioned between the issuers and the investors of securities.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Financial+Crisis+Inquiry+Report&amp;rft.pages=43-44&amp;rft.pub=National+Commission+on+the+Causes+of+the+Financial+and+Economic+Crisis+in+the+United+States&amp;rft.date=2011&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.gpo.gov%2Ffdsys%2Fpkg%2FGPO-FCIC%2Fpdf%2FGPO-FCIC.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ACredit+rating+agency" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-controversy_SF-32"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-controversy_SF_32-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web">Alessi, Christopher. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.cfr.org/united-states/credit-rating-controversy/p22328">"The Credit Rating Controversy. Archived from <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.bloomberg.com/apps/news?pid=newsarchive&amp;sid=au4oIx.judz4">the original</a> on October 17, 2015. <q>Moody\xe2\x80\x99s, the only one of the three that stands alone as a publicly traded company, has averaged pretax profit margins of 52 percent over the past five years. It reported revenue of $1.76 billion &#8211; earning a pretax margin of 41 percent &#8211; even during the economic collapse in 2008. S&amp;P, Moody\xe2\x80\x99s and Fitch control 98 percent of the market for debt ratings in the U.S., according to the SEC. The noncompetitive market leads to high fees, says SEC Commissioner Casey, 43, appointed by President George W. Bush in July 2006 to a five-year term. S&amp;P, a unit of McGraw-Hill Cos., has profit margins similar to those at Moody\xe2\x80\x99s, she says.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Bloomberg&amp;rft.atitle=Flawed+Credit+Ratings+Reap+Profits+as+Regulators+Fail+%28Update1%29&amp;rft.date=2009-04-29&amp;rft.aulast=Evans&amp;rft.aufirst=David&amp;rft.au=Caroline+Salas&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.bloomberg.com%2Fapps%2Fnews%3Fpid%3Dnewsarchive%26sid%3Dau4oIx.judz4&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ACredit+rating+agency" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/> </span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-38"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-38">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation news">Younglai, Rachelle; daCosta, Ana (2 August 2011). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.reuters.com/article/2011/08/02/us-ratings-insight-idUSTRE7714TI20110802">"Insight: When ratings agencies judge the world"</a>. <i>Reuters</i><span class="reference-accessdate">. International Monetary Fund. October 2010. p.&#160;2. <q>According to the theoretical literature, CRAs potentially provide information, monitoring, and certification services. First, since investors do not often know as much as issuers about the factors that determine credit quality, credit ratings address an important problem of asymmetric information between debt issuers and investors. Hence, CRAs provide an independent evaluation and assessment of the ability of issuers to meet their debt obligations. In this way, CRAs provide `information services` that reduce information costs, increase the pool of potential borrowers, and promote liquid markets.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Global+Financial+Stability+Report+Chapter+3%3A+The+Uses+and+Abuses+of+Sovereign+Credit+Ratings&amp;rft.pages=2&amp;rft.pub=International+Monetary+Fund&amp;rft.date=2010-10&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.imf.org%2Fexternal%2Fpubs%2Fft%2Fgfsr%2F2010%2F02%2Fpdf%2Fchap3.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ACredit+rating+agency" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-Sinclair_05-pay-58"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Sinclair_05-pay_58-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book"><a href="/wiki/Timothy_J._Sinclair" title="Timothy J. Portfolio Penguin. pp.&#160;113\xe2\x80\x93114. <q>The agencies had charts and studies showing that their ratings were accurate a very high percentage of the time. But anyone who dig more deeply could find many instances when they got it wrong, usually when something unexpected happened. The rating agencies had missed the near default of New York City, the bankruptcy of Orange County, and the Asian and Russian meltdowns. They failed to catch Penn Central in the 1970s and Long-Term Capital Management in the 1990s. They often downgraded companies just days before bankruptcy &#8211; too late to help investors. Nor was this anything new: one study showed that 78% of the municipal bonds rated double A or triple-A in 1929 defaulted during the Great Depression.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=All+the+Devils+Are+Here&amp;rft.pages=113-114&amp;rft.pub=Portfolio+Penguin&amp;rft.date=2010&amp;rft.aulast=McLean&amp;rft.aufirst=Bethany&amp;rft.au=Joe+Nocera&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ACredit+rating+agency" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-McLean113-88"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-McLean113_88-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Bethany McLean; Joe Nocera (2010). <i>All the Devils Are Here, the Hidden History of the Financial Crisis</i>. National Commission on the Causes of the Financial and Economic Crisis in the United States. 2011. p.&#160;44. <q>Participants in the securitization industry realized that they needed to secure favorable credit ratings in order to sell structured products to investors. This American Life (radio program) from WBEZ<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">3 September</span> 2013</span>. <q>Adam Davidson: And by the way, before you finance enthusiasts start writing any letters, we do know that $70 trillion technically refers to that subset of global savings called fixed income securities. ... Ceyla Pazarbasioglu: This number doubled since 2000. In 2000 this was about $36 trillion. Adam Davidson: So it took several hundred years for the world to get to $36 trillion. And then it took six years to get another $36 trillion.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=Originally+aired+05.09.2008&amp;rft.atitle=Giant+Pool+of+Money+%28transcript%29&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.thisamericanlife.org%2Fradio-archives%2Fepisode%2F355%2Ftranscript&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ACredit+rating+agency" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-129"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-129">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In the case of the one CRA that was a separate public company &#8211; Moody\'s &#8211; "Between the time it was spun off into a public company and February 2007, its stock had risen 340%. National Commission on the Causes of the Financial and Economic Crisis in the United States. 2011. p.&#160;xxv.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Financial+Crisis+Inquiry+Report&amp;rft.pages=xxv&amp;rft.pub=National+Commission+on+the+Causes+of+the+Financial+and+Economic+Crisis+in+the+United+States&amp;rft.date=2011&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.gpo.gov%2Ffdsys%2Fpkg%2FGPO-FCIC%2Fpdf%2FGPO-FCIC.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ACredit+rating+agency" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-131"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-131">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">70%. "Firms bought mortgage-backed bonds with the very highest yields they could find and reassembled them into new CDOs. The original bonds ... could be lower-rated securities that once reassembled into a new CDO would wind up with as much as 70% of the tranches rated triple-A. Ratings arbitrage, Wall Street called this practice. A more accurate term would have been ratings laundering." (source: McLean and Nocera, <i>All the Devils Are Here</i>, 2010 p.122)</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-132"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-132">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">80%. "In a CDO you gathered a 100 different mortgage bonds \xe2\x80\x94 usually the riskiest lower floors of the original tower ...... They bear a lower credit rating triple B. ... if you could somehow get them rerated as triple A, thereby lowering their perceived risk, however dishonestly and artificially. This is what Goldman Sachs had cleverly done. it was absurd. The 100 buildings occupied the same floodplain; in the event of flood, the ground floors of all of them were equally exposed. But never mind: the rating agencies, who were paid fat fees by Goldman Sachs and other Wall Street firms for each deal they rated, pronounced 80% of the new tower of debt triple-A." (source: Michael Lewis, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Big_Short" title="The Big Short">The Big Short</a>&#160;: Inside the Doomsday Machine</i> WW Norton and Co, 2010, p.73)</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-133"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-133">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"Unlike the traditional cash CDO, synthetic CDOs contained no actual tranches of mortgage-backed securities ... in the place of real mortgage assets, these CDOs contained credit default swaps and did not finance a single home purchase." Sandage (Harvard University Press, 2005), chapters 4\xe2\x80\x936.</li>\n<li>On contemporary dynamics, see Timothy J. Sinclair, <i>The New Masters of Capital: American Bond Rating Agencies and the Politics of Creditworthiness</i> (Ithaca, NY: Cornell University Press, 2005).</li>\n<li>For a description of what CRAs do in the corporate context, see <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.iosco.org/library/pubdocs/pdf/IOSCOPD153.pdf">IOSCO Report on the Activities of Credit Rating Agencies</a> and <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.iosco.org/library/pubdocs/pdf/IOSCOPD151.pdf">IOSCO Statement of Principles Regarding the Activities of Credit Rating Agencies</a>.</li>\n<li>On the limits of the current \'Issuer-pays\' business model, see Kenneth C. Kettering, Securization and its discontents: The Dynamics of Financial Product Development, 29 CDZLR 1553, 60 (2008).</li>\n<li>For a renewed approach of CRAs business model, see Vincent Fabi\xc3\xa9, A Rescue Plan for rating Agencies, Blue Sky\xe2\x80\x94New Ideas for the Obama Administration <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20090615005411/http://ideas.berkeleylawblogs.org/2009/04/19/a-rescue-plan-for-rating-agencies/">ideas.berkeleylawblogs.org</a>.</li>\n<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://papers.ssrn.com/sol3/papers.cfm?abstract_id=1431994">Frank J. Fabozzi and Dennis Vink (2009). "On securitization and over-reliance on credit ratings". <i>Yale International Center for Finance.</i></a></li>\n<li>For a theoretical analysis of the impact of regulation on rating agencies\' business model, see <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://ssrn.com/abstract=1540099">Rating Agencies in the Face of Regulation\xe2\x80\x94Rating Inflation and Regulatory Arbitrage, by Opp, Christian C., Opp, Marcus M. and Harris, Milton (2010).</a></li>\n<li>Analysts and ratings = chapter 14 in <i>Stocks and Exchange \xe2\x80\x93 the only Book you need</i>, Ladis Konecny, 2013, <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9783848220656" title="Special:BookSources/9783848220656">9783848220656</a>.</li>\n<li>For an historical account of the interaction between a government and the rating agencies, see David James Gill, "Rating the UK: the British government\'s sovereign credit ratings, 1976\xe2\x80\x9378," <i>Economic History Review</i>, Vol. 68, No. 3 (2015), pp.&#160;1016\xe2\x80\x931037.</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline"
